  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_068e2602-935e-4a14-899e-5e7294b68bed'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer317549289" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8533132232192854605"><b>
  <u>The Cover :</u>
</b> Honestly if my reading group had not choosen Finding Sky as part of it monthly read I might not have otherwise have read it. Now don’t misunderstand me, the art decoration is so simple… well not simple…elegant is a better word to use. The vine used with what looks like ribbon to intertwine a heart gives no indication as to what lies beneath the cover other that a possible romance of some kind.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>The Characters :</u>
</b> Every book has them, heck without them the story would not have mad</span>
  <span id="freeText8533132232192854605" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>The Cover :</u>
</b> Honestly if my reading group had not choosen Finding Sky as part of it monthly read I might not have otherwise have read it. Now don’t misunderstand me, the art decoration is so simple… well not simple…elegant is a better word to use. The vine used with what looks like ribbon to intertwine a heart gives no indication as to what lies beneath the cover other that a possible romance of some kind.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>The Characters :</u>
</b> Every book has them, heck without them the story would not have made it print. Well then again, it might have but I would not be interested in reading it. So, moving on we dive into the charming and some possibly not so charming characters of “Finding Sky”.<br /><br />Guard your hearts ladies first up is the male lead!! Why you ask?? It’s simple, because it’s important to see if “Zed” is book boyfriend material. Why else? And the verdict is a solid yes. What girl, American or British can pass up a bad boy on a motorcycle? And to make him even yummier we find out that he has a heart of gold. Yes, ladies break out the fans because this is one bad boy we want our bad boys to reflect. <br /><br /><br />Don’t worry my fair gents, I didn’t forget you, I’m sure you want to know if Sky Bright is girlfriend material. Being that well, umm…. I’m not a guy or into girls; I would still hand the verdict down as a solid yes. Yes she may seem weak and withdrawn at times, but who wouldn’t with the shit she has suffered through. But when it comes down to protecting the ones she loves I think she has what it takes. <br /><br />Speaking of delicious characters and whether they are bf/gf material believe it or not “Finding Sky” has other characters besides Zed &amp; Sky. The thing is if you really want to know if they bring the goods you are just going to have to read it…. after all I did. But I will give you a quick rundown.<br /><br />I have to start with <b>
  <u>Nelson:</u>
</b> Sky human super hero… He is the kind of guy you want as your bff in high school. He’s always ready to take the stand for a woman’s honor. I was so glad the author found him love. I would have been disappointed had he not been rewarded. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>Tina:</u>
</b> Tina is a first person to friend sky and become part of a side line story that is interesting. I was disappointed that it didn’t dig deeper.<br /> <br />And last but not least <b>
  <u>The Benedict Brothers :</u>
</b> Yes you heard me….plural— BROTHERS!! There are six other and I have a feeling they are all going to be yummy. Though we only get a peek at few of them as they play important roles in the story line. I can’t wait as the series continues and we get a chance to get up close and personal as they find their soul finders.<br /><br />If you were to ask me, “Lissa did you like the book?” I would have to respond…. Did I like the book??? Are you completely mad??? I absolutely loved the book Zed turns out to b absolutely delicious I put my own order for a copy of Zed. I’m a bit disappointed he hasn’t showed up yet. With my luck it was the answering machine I got and the message was deleted. <br /><br /><b>
  <u> My recommendation: </u>
</b>Okay woman of all ages and guys who can handle a little chic lit…. run— don’t walk to your computer and log on to Amazon or B&amp;N accounts and pick up your copy today…. Paperback, Nook or kindle no matter your vice they have pretty much anything. <br /><br /><b>Remember be kind “like” my review before leave!!<br /></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="8533132232192854605" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_700268609" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/700268609" />
    <a title="krisy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8758945-krisy"><img alt="krisy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1439570951p2/8758945.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/700268609?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="krisy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="krisy" href="/user/show/8758945-krisy">krisy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780192792952" href="/book/show/9849587-finding-sky">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people who aren't looking for anything new and original</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8758945-krisy?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer700268609" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10243012457253803059">Only 35 people, apart from me, gave this book one star. Wow. I feel like a special snowflake.<br/><br/>I gotta mention that I got this book as a birthday present from my best friends regardless of the fact that I told them not to buy me anything because I wasn't even home for my birthday. But they bought me a tiny ceramic tree with amethyst leaves, which I loved, and this book - not so much. I assume that they either have no idea what I like to read or simply hate me. Maybe both.<br/><br/>Now, let's get straight to</span>
  <span id="freeText10243012457253803059" style="display:none">Only 35 people, apart from me, gave this book one star. Wow. I feel like a special snowflake.<br><br>I gotta mention that I got this book as a birthday present from my best friends regardless of the fact that I told them not to buy me anything because I wasn't even home for my birthday. But they bought me a tiny ceramic tree with amethyst leaves, which I loved, and this book - not so much. I assume that they either have no idea what I like to read or simply hate me. Maybe both.<br><br>Now, let's get straight to my thoughts on this book.<br>All in all,<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380433836i/873345._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>For some reason, this book pissed me off. I guess the main reason is that I had low expectations about it anyway. And because it was SO. FUCKING. UNORIGINAL. I would have given it two stars if it wasn't so annoyingly unoriginal and lacked atmosphere. I gave two stars to <i>Shiver</i> which felt like over-sweetened tea, while this book felt like cold noodles. And I just really don't like cold noodles. No offence for the fans, but that's just how I felt it.<br><br>Like I said, I found this book pretty unoriginal. It sounded like some Twilight rip-off. Even my cousin, who hasn't read a single book in the last 5 years apart from the ones she needed for school assignments, read the blurb, handed the book to me and hissed 'Do they even have any new ideas?' (And if you're gonna tell me that this book is perfect for the Twilight fans, um, sorry, I might have enjoyed Twilight, but it doesn't mean that I'd want to read another cheesy book about ~new girl in new school runs into the love of her lyf.)<br><br>Girl moves from far, far away and has to get used to the new school? Check. Considers herself a freak? Check. Said girl sees a mysterious guy and develops a crush on him and is pretty sure he hates her because he ignores her? Check. Mysterious guy actually does mysterious things and acts like a confused drug addict? Check. Mysterious guy suddenly becomes a sweetheart? Do I need to go on?<br><br>The difference is that when Twilight came out, this storyline wasn't overused, and Twilight actually has aura and that haunting atmosphere and feels like chocolate and mint and I accidentally sold my soul to Stephenie Meyer a few years ago, so let's not get to this topic because I don't want to get all sappy.<br><br>Sky was bugging me the whole time. Yeah, I know that she has this emotional trauma and has to distract her mind somehow, but being inside her head was hard to bear at times. She seemed too naive, one-dimensional at times, and, let's face it, plain stupid. Why would you believe some creepy guy who hands you a bag that's not yours with the words 'There's a photo of you in it'. Um. I didn't like Zed that much, either. I didn't find him as swoony as everyone says. Plus, I bet he wouldn't even have tried to notice Sky if it wasn't the football game. What annoyed me the most is how stalker-ish he got when he found out that ~~~~she's her soulmate wow baby we'll be together for the rest of our lives ehehehe~~~~. If I were to be in Sky's place, I would've stabbed Zed with a fork. Oh, and the minor characters. As much as I like them, ALL of them are one-dimensional.<br><br>The whole thing with the gifts didn't make sense to me at times. Apart from the fact that I wouldn't want a boyfriend who can constantly read my mind, everything was a little bit over the place. I found Zed's 'I can see the future but I don't see it clearly and it's almost never certain and I can't see your future when you're with me' gift pretty useless. And I didn't really understand how he could always read her mind when she was thinking about something embarrassing/too personal, but not when she had some actually pretty important thoughts crossing her mind.<br><br>The FBI thing was simply absurd. That's when I said to myself 'there goes your second star'. Don't even get me started about the abduction. It was so ridiculous, Jesus.<br><br>And now, you might say, after you've disliked everything else about this book, at least you might have liked the writing? No. I can't really tell you why, but I found the writing style somehow... I don't know, too ordinary. The author never made me tear up, go all AWWW, feel surprised by some of the plot twists (if there were any?) or at least feel Sky's pain. I don't know if I had lost my ability to get emotional over fictional characters, or this book just didn't do its job.<br><br>I know that a lot of people liked this story, but to me it was, well, too lame.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10243012457253803059" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer115674617" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9977842077973268791">(3.5stars)<br/><br/>TBR Reduce Challenge #8- 2011 (Alexa) <br/><br/><i>"You have half our gifts, I the other. Together we make a whole. Together we are much more powerful."</i><br/><br/>English girl, Sky Bright, just moved to Colorado since her adopted parents got a new job teaching at an art center in town.<br/>Sky has always had a complicated life. She was abandoned at a motorway service station when she was six, traumatized and not being able to remember her own name. And while life seems to be better now, it all changes when she mee</span>
  <span id="freeText9977842077973268791" style="display:none">(3.5stars)<br /><br />TBR Reduce Challenge #8- 2011 (Alexa) <br /><br /><i>"You have half our gifts, I the other. Together we make a whole. Together we are much more powerful."</i><br /><br />English girl, Sky Bright, just moved to Colorado since her adopted parents got a new job teaching at an art center in town.<br />Sky has always had a complicated life. She was abandoned at a motorway service station when she was six, traumatized and not being able to remember her own name. And while life seems to be better now, it all changes when she meets Zed Benedict, someone that can link her, to her past and hold her future.<br /><br />To be honest, I wasn't sure if I was going to finish this one. It took so long to get into the writing style and plot line, but once things started happening with Sky and Zed and the paranormal elements started taking shape, it got really interesting.<br /><br />For the most part I really liked the characters. Sky Bright? Okay, I hate her name, but she's a sweet, shy and cute girl, but I liked her a lot more once she started believing in herself more.<br />Zed's a pretty complex thing now isn't he? Like Sky, it was hard to adjust to his sudden rage to romance, but eventually I started to like this Zed much better.<br />Together they were a very sweet touching couple, mind you the dialog was a bit cheesy, but it was nice none the less.<br /><br />My favorite part was the elements laced in this one. I liked the idea of Savant, how they became, what they can do and the twist with the soulfinders was pretty great as well. It wasn't overly unique, but definitely different. <br /><br />Overall, I enjoyed <b>Finding Sky</b>. It had some really sweet moments, some grip and was a fun entertaining and intriguing read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9977842077973268791" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15248618908375456150">Amazing. This was one of those stumbled- upon gems of a book. It's even hard for me to pinpoint exactly why I love it so much because so much of this book is very standard fare these days: paranormal girl meets boy with a wonderful family who saves her romance type stuff. . It just has that extra kick that makes you fall in love with a book. Loved Sky- vulnerable, tough, sweet. I want the Benedicts to adopt me. Please please! I loved the way Stirling gave Sky a difficult past without making her </span>
  <span id="freeText15248618908375456150" style="display:none">Amazing. This was one of those stumbled- upon gems of a book. It's even hard for me to pinpoint exactly why I love it so much because so much of this book is very standard fare these days: paranormal girl meets boy with a wonderful family who saves her romance type stuff. . It just has that extra kick that makes you fall in love with a book. Loved Sky- vulnerable, tough, sweet. I want the Benedicts to adopt me. Please please! I loved the way Stirling gave Sky a difficult past without making her into a pitiable victim. The romance was well done too, which surprised me because normally I wouldn't find the male romatic lead character type very compelling. Her mythology is very well-rounded and unique, too. But she does an excellent job here. A really worthwhile read. I will definitely read the next one.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15435218878069066195">You weird, weird book...I think this annoyed me to the same extent as I liked it...<br/><br/>BUT - first off: I want to say THANK YOU dear JoJo for sending me this book! Thank you so much! ♥<br/><br/>Now, what did I think of this? I must say, Finding Sky felt like a rather clumsy attempt at paranormal YA romance. <i>Clumsy</i> because there were just so many things that didn't make any sense to me at all - I'm sure I've got additional wrinkles on my forehead now because of all my frowning - and an <i>attempt</i> because...well..</span>
  <span id="freeText15435218878069066195" style="display:none">You weird, weird book...I think this annoyed me to the same extent as I liked it...<br /><br />BUT - first off: I want to say THANK YOU dear JoJo for sending me this book! Thank you so much! ♥<br /><br />Now, what did I think of this? I must say, Finding Sky felt like a rather clumsy attempt at paranormal YA romance. <i>Clumsy</i> because there were just so many things that didn't make any sense to me at all - I'm sure I've got additional wrinkles on my forehead now because of all my frowning - and an <i>attempt</i> because...well...there wasn't any chemistry whatsoever between the two main characters. Every potentially steamy moment was cut off - and this rather bluntly - by the author, which frustrated me beyond all measure. Unfortunately, I can't even give any brownie points for the bad boy :( He just wasn't swoon-worthy enough. The change from YOU-CAN-ROT-IN-HELL-FOR-ALL-I-CARE to OMG-I-LOVE-YOU-SO-YOU-ARE-MY-LIFE-MY-DESTINY-MY-EVERYTHING was so abrupt I almost got a whiplash. This wasn't completely horrible; I finished it fairly quickly and it did entertain me but as much as I would have loved to love this - seeing as I got it as a gift and I feel bad about ripping into it - I just couldn't. :(</span>

<div id="review_127958337" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/127958337" />
    <a title="Meg Moggs" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4199137-meg-moggs"><img alt="Meg Moggs" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582814264p2/4199137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/127958337?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meg Moggs" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meg Moggs" href="/user/show/4199137-meg-moggs">Meg Moggs</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4199137-meg-moggs?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4199137-meg-moggs?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4199137-meg-moggs?shelf=paranormal-supernatural">paranormal-supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4199137-meg-moggs?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4199137-meg-moggs?shelf=psychics">psychics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer127958337" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16612568020692370164">When I first saw this book, I wasn't going to bother reading it. The blurb makes it out to be cliché and over the top, and I didn't fancy another Twilight. But still, I gave it a try and bought it. So one rainy afternoon, while I was still feeling lost after finishing my beloved L.J.Snith novel, I decided to read this. I was gripped from the first chapter. It had an intriguing start, and had a nice feeling of normality to it.<br/><br/>It starts off by warming us to the characters: Sky, her adoptive parent</span>
  <span id="freeText16612568020692370164" style="display:none">When I first saw this book, I wasn't going to bother reading it. The blurb makes it out to be cliché and over the top, and I didn't fancy another Twilight. But still, I gave it a try and bought it. So one rainy afternoon, while I was still feeling lost after finishing my beloved L.J.Snith novel, I decided to read this. I was gripped from the first chapter. It had an intriguing start, and had a nice feeling of normality to it.<br /><br />It starts off by warming us to the characters: Sky, her adoptive parents and her new friend Tina at her new American school. It follows Sky through her day to day school-life as she tries to fit in. Then, Zed Benedict is introduced. At first, he seems like just another wannabe tough guy. He's cool, rebellious and a jerk. But then at a football match, Sky replies to the voice she hears in her head-Zed's. This is when he realizes she is a Savant, and his Soulfinder, the perfect match Savants search for all their lives.<br /><br />I like the way Sky finds it all hard to believe; too often in paranormal romances the girl is usually taken by the guy staright away and believes ever word he says. Well, that's not realistic at all, is it? But Zed gives up trying to convince her and after some time asks her out. They are just a normal couple for a while, but then they get shot at in the woods. This is when the Benedicts (a family of 7 brothers and their parents, Zed is the youngest) realize the danger they are in. Someone is out to get them.<br /><br />Zed and Sky don't get to see eachother that often, but when Sky is taken by an evil Savant, she starts to unlock her true powers, and realizes exactly how much Zed means to her. Together, they uncover her dark past and face the co-operation that wants the Benedicts dead. <br /><br />All in all, an exciting, realistic novel full of twists. I hope there is a sequel, but if there isn't one, I'm happy in the knowledge that there was a satisfying ending.<br />- Zanthie ;)</span>
  <a data-text-id="16612568020692370164" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_182770107" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/182770107" />
    <a title="Bungle Midnight Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3619262-bungle-midnight-reads"><img alt="Bungle Midnight Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310061930p2/3619262.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/182770107?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bungle Midnight Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bungle Midnight Reads" href="/user/show/3619262-bungle-midnight-reads">Bungle Midnight Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer182770107" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9470826550095499664">WOW! Just WOW! Why didn't I read this book sooner?<br/><br/><br/>I think the above, taken from goodreads, tells you enough about the book and I kinda wish something similar was written on the back of the book itself.<br/>I will admit this is a book I looked at over and over in work and for some reason I never bought it. But then one of my customers couldn't stop talking about it and we have very similar tastes. Before I had chance to buy the book she had come back into the shop and said 'read it, you'll love it' an</span>
  <span id="freeText9470826550095499664" style="display:none">WOW! Just WOW! Why didn't I read this book sooner?<br /><br /><br />I think the above, taken from goodreads, tells you enough about the book and I kinda wish something similar was written on the back of the book itself.<br />I will admit this is a book I looked at over and over in work and for some reason I never bought it. But then one of my customers couldn't stop talking about it and we have very similar tastes. Before I had chance to buy the book she had come back into the shop and said 'read it, you'll love it' and boy did I love it!<br /><br /><br />Finding Sky is a story that pulls at your heart strings as you are dragged into Sky's world and the journey she is on to find herself and understand her past. Her past is locked deep in her mind and only her Savant and his family can help her unlock the doors.<br />I really like Sky, sure she has troubling dealing with what Zed has to tell her, who wouldn't, and yes she may have trouble dealing with her past but she isn't weak and I love how she grows throughout the story. She allows herself to finally let go and trust Zed and his family as they help her on her path to discovery/recovery.<br /><br /><br />And now for Zed *swoons a little* (sorry, I couldn't help myself). He is everything I want in a leading man. He is strong, protective, and arrogant, as well as loving and caring. He would do anything to protect Sky. But Zed also has his own demons to deal with and he needs his Savant just as much as she needs him. <br />The relationship between Zed and Sky develops at a nice pace and I hope to hear more from them throughout the other brother's books.<br /><br /><br />Speaking about the other brothers, Zed comes from a large family, he is the seventh son, and his brothers are all great characters. You feel each of them has a real purpose and I can't wait to read each of their books!<br />I think that is actually what I'm going to love most about this series, each brother is going to get his own story but we still get the rest of the family.<br /><br /><br />Stirling has created a world I would happily get lost in! Let me know if you feel the same!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9470826550095499664" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2168725203" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10514437725721901129">This is another really light and non engaging paranormal book. Honestly it was nothing too special and I don't think I'll remember it for a very long time, but while I was reading it it was lots of fun. It was a very light and I read it in 3 hours. That's not normal for me. It usually takes me a lot more, but this book was just so addicting.<br/>It pretty much stars like every paranormal book. The main female character moves to a small town where she meets a mysterious bad boy. The boy of course is r</span>
  <span id="freeText10514437725721901129" style="display:none">This is another really light and non engaging paranormal book. Honestly it was nothing too special and I don't think I'll remember it for a very long time, but while I was reading it it was lots of fun. It was a very light and I read it in 3 hours. That's not normal for me. It usually takes me a lot more, but this book was just so addicting.<br />It pretty much stars like every paranormal book. The main female character moves to a small town where she meets a mysterious bad boy. The boy of course is really hot and also hides lots of secrets. So far it doesn't sound like something original. To be honest it isn't. Especially the beginning is really cliche and it pretty much stays like that, but I don't know I still liked it.<br />First off all I like how she found out his abilities. In most paranormal book I've read the heroine finds out by accident or in some weird way, but here he just tells her. I don't know why, but I really liked it. Trying to picture her expression. <br />Also I really liked the scene when they were playing football. As someone that can't even hit the ball, I found it really relatable.<br />But I can't deny that their whole relationship was insta love. That did bother me, but I was expecting so it didn't ruin the book.<br />So overall I liked the book. Nothing special, but fun</span>
  <a data-text-id="10514437725721901129" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1407870793" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer4506205847123988209"><b> Actual Rating: 4.25 </b><br/><br/>This was a great read. The story contained just the right amount of romance and mystery. The story was interesting and fun to read. It is about a girl named Sky who was left at the age of 10 and she is adopted. Her adopted parents move to America and she has to make a new life, and friends. As the time passes, she makes new friends and has an attraction towards Zed Benedict. <br/><br/>The characters were great. Sky is really down-to-earth. She is also shy and cute. Zed is the biker ba</span>
  <span id="freeText4506205847123988209" style="display:none"><b> Actual Rating: 4.25 </b><br /><br />This was a great read. The story contained just the right amount of romance and mystery. The story was interesting and fun to read. It is about a girl named Sky who was left at the age of 10 and she is adopted. Her adopted parents move to America and she has to make a new life, and friends. As the time passes, she makes new friends and has an attraction towards Zed Benedict. <br /><br />The characters were great. Sky is really down-to-earth. She is also shy and cute. Zed is the biker bad boy. He may look tough on the outside, but he actually has a heart of gold. I love their parents. They were so sweet and cool. Zed's family is odd because they have superpowers and apparent Sky does too. She is Zed's soulfinder (aka soul mate).<br /><br />The action made the book interesting. I hope the other books continue keeps up the excitement of this book. Can't wait to read the rest of the series. Overall, a great young adult romance. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4506205847123988209" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer14734214283699998031">Love this book. I was hooked straight away. The characters were described so well and having a book with a completely different topic from the norm was great. Savents never heard of them but i am presuming that they may become a big topic because they are a whole new area of people with a mystery and so not completely human as we know it. Sky is a great heroine. The book is set around her having an intense journey not only to another country but love and a whole side of herself which she has nev</span>
  <span id="freeText14734214283699998031" style="display:none">Love this book. I was hooked straight away. The characters were described so well and having a book with a completely different topic from the norm was great. Savents never heard of them but i am presuming that they may become a big topic because they are a whole new area of people with a mystery and so not completely human as we know it. Sky is a great heroine. The book is set around her having an intense journey not only to another country but love and a whole side of herself which she has never dreamed of. She didn't fall straight for Zed (not intentionally) but she is just drawn to him. She ends up questioning all she knows and wants. I also love her background in the book she has complex problems which take the whole book to level. I love some of Joss's metaphores 'an alice that never made it back through the looking glass.' Deffinatly looking forward to the sequal Stealing Phoenix. It may not have Sky and Zed in as the main couple but instead Yves and Phoneix. Although, apparently Sky and Zed do play an important part. She is a modern heroine who does not want to be ordered about by her prince charming but she takes command and makes her own choices and has a plan in life which will not end with love. i deffinatly reccomend this book it is just brilliant. I can't wait to discover more.</span>

<div id="review_121809386" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/121809386" />
    <a title="Kelly/yllektra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2681812-kelly-yllektra"><img alt="Kelly/yllektra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1286130063p2/2681812.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/121809386?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly/yllektra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly/yllektra" href="/user/show/2681812-kelly-yllektra">Kelly/yllektra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer121809386&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer121809386" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5419579193111848002">I finished this book today. It might have taken me 3 days but that was mostly due to prior engagements I couldn't get out of. <br/><br/>I caught a special edition of this book with an extra poster which was lovely and I do think the cover is really nice. That is what drew me to it, initially. <br/><br/>When I started reading it, I didn't know exactly what to expect, but it didn't disappoint.<br/><br/>As a non-native English speaker I always rejoice at the opportunity to read a book that is written in "decorative language" wi</span>
  <span id="freeText5419579193111848002" style="display:none">I finished this book today. It might have taken me 3 days but that was mostly due to prior engagements I couldn't get out of. <br /><br />I caught a special edition of this book with an extra poster which was lovely and I do think the cover is really nice. That is what drew me to it, initially. <br /><br />When I started reading it, I didn't know exactly what to expect, but it didn't disappoint.<br /><br />As a non-native English speaker I always rejoice at the opportunity to read a book that is written in "decorative language" with lots of descriptions and adjectives etc, but this book was written in a simple way.<br />Yet, it didn't make it any less enjoyable. Actually, I found myself smiling and grinning every other page mostly. It was THAT fun.<br /><br />I liked the situations Sky got herself into and how real her reactions and her peers' reactions were to everything. She felt really normal...<br />But she wasn't..exactly normal.<br /><br />Sky is a girl who has no memory of her past. She just knows it wasn't pleasant and that whoever had her, left her because she was bad and undeserving of love. She also had a unique ability, gift if you may, to be able to sense and see the true feelings of everyone around her. Their auras as she said. Each emotion has a different color and no one can hide. This ability gave her a compass which she used in order to keep herself safe.<br /><br />She was adopted by Sally and Simon, an English couple of artists who were kind and patient enough to take her in when she barely spoke. It took her a lot of time to come out of her shell but she did.<br /><br />When they moved to Colorado, Sky didn't know what to anticipate but she made friends easily, Tina and Nelson mostly.<br />Then, there was this dark, broody boy with a relatively ambiguous reputation. The bad boy. Zed. <br /><br />Every girl lusts after him, and Sky finds herself fascinated but he is too mysterious and dangerous for her taste, so she tries to dismiss it.<br /><br />I actually liked that about her. I mean it was a completely natural reaction. I liked the fact that she kept her cool and even though she wanted him, she didn't like him. I loved that distinction and I loved that she was straight with him too.<br /><br />It's only during a soccer game that the secret is revealed. Zed is a Savant and tries to help her telepathically in a situation,without knowing that Sky is a telepath too and could hear him. Actually, not even Sky knew it!<br />It appears that Savants are people with several abilities, like telekinesis, or pyrokinesis , or healing...<br /><br />But after that, Zed tells her she is his "Soulfinder" - his absolute soulmate for eternity- and he knew that because: "When a Soulfinder speaks telepathically to her partner, it's like all the lights coming on in a building. You lit me up like Vegas".<br /><br />Sky is unconvinced and gives him a hard time, because predetermination isn't something she likes, but gradually she comes to realize that they do share a deeper, connection that cannot be explained. They really are soulmates.<br /><br />Throw in a family of evil Savants wanting to take revenge against the Benedicts (Zed's family of 9) for solving crimes for the Police, brainwash etc and you have a very exciting novel.<br />We also do find out some of Sky's past, but it is pretty unclear so we need a sequel!!!<br /><br />I'm eagerly waiting for the next one! :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="5419579193111848002" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_125929821" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/125929821" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3344685-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388694025p2/3344685.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/125929821?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/3344685-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=british-author">british-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=books-i-own-print">books-i-own-print</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=for-review-read">for-review-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer125929821" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12188205054946529155">Sky has lived with her adoptive parents since she was 10 years old and remembers little of her life before she was with them. Her parents have been offered jobs running a new arts centre in Colorado and although this means the family leaving their home in Richmond, England they are excited about moving to America. Sky is beginning to settle into her new school and finds herself drawn to the school bad boy Zed. At first he ignores her but then she starts hearing his voice in her head and she thin</span>
  <span id="freeText12188205054946529155" style="display:none">Sky has lived with her adoptive parents since she was 10 years old and remembers little of her life before she was with them. Her parents have been offered jobs running a new arts centre in Colorado and although this means the family leaving their home in Richmond, England they are excited about moving to America. Sky is beginning to settle into her new school and finds herself drawn to the school bad boy Zed. At first he ignores her but then she starts hearing his voice in her head and she thinks she is losing her mind. Is there an explanation for everything that is happening? Will Sky accept it when Zed tells her they are soul mates?<br /><br />Finding Sky is a great debut and one that stands out in a crowded young adult paranormal romance market. Although I love stories about vampires, werewolves and angels they do seem to have overtaken the shelves at the moment so it makes a refreshing change to read a story about characters with psychic abilities. Sky has no idea that she is a savant so when Zed starts talking to her about her abilities and the fact that she is his soulfinder she doesn't believe him at first. It takes time for him to gain her trust and for her to accept the things he is telling her.<br /><br />I was a little worried that the fact they are soul mates would mean they were instantly in love and a happy couple before you could blink so it was nice to see how slowly things developed between them. The romance is sweet, quite amusing in places and just a joy to read. In fact I'd happily have continued reading if only there had been more pages.<br /><br />One of the things I liked the most was the fact that both Sky and Zed have supportive families. Sky may not remember her real parents but her adoptive parents both care for her a great deal and are prepared to do anything to help her. I liked the fact that they were prepared to give up their dreams and move back to England if that was what Sky wanted. Zed's family were great, his parents and 6 brothers are all savants with a variety of different psychic abilities that I enjoyed learning about. I loved the banter between them all and watching them together was like watching any family - there were squabbles but when it came down to it they all love each other and will always stick together.<br /><br />I want to know more about each of the Benedict brothers so I'm really hoping this turns into a series and we get to see each of their stories. I was pleased to find out Joss Stirling is currently working on a sequel called Stealing Phoenix and I'm very much looking forward to reading it as soon as it comes out. If you enjoy paranormal romance but are looking for something that is fresh and exciting then you can't go far wrong with Finding Sky!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12188205054946529155" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_635743735" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/635743735" />
    <a title="Christie«SHBBblogger»" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6650940-christie-shbbblogger"><img alt="Christie«SHBBblogger»" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537729030p2/6650940.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/635743735?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christie«SHBBblogger»" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christie«SHBBblogger»" href="/user/show/6650940-christie-shbbblogger">Christie«SHBBblogger»</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780192732521" href="/book/show/9418083-finding-sky">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6650940-christie-shbbblogger?shelf=abused-in-childhood">abused-in-childhood</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6650940-christie-shbbblogger?shelf=superpowers-galore">superpowers-galore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6650940-christie-shbbblogger?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6650940-christie-shbbblogger?shelf=pnr">pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6650940-christie-shbbblogger?shelf=na">na</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6650940-christie-shbbblogger?shelf=insta-love">insta-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer635743735" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12880984748444021816">Yes, yes, yes! This is exactly what I didn't know I was looking for. I haven't read PNR in quite a while. I've kind of unintentionally drifted away from it but this was so refreshing at a time when it seems like nothing I read has been satisfying. I started reading this with no expectations but from the first page, the descriptive, almost poetic writing about the Colorado mountains really drew me in. <br/><br/>The main idea behind this story is this: there are people out there with extra sensory abilities</span>
  <span id="freeText12880984748444021816" style="display:none">Yes, yes, yes! This is exactly what I didn't know I was looking for. I haven't read PNR in quite a while. I've kind of unintentionally drifted away from it but this was so refreshing at a time when it seems like nothing I read has been satisfying. I started reading this with no expectations but from the first page, the descriptive, almost poetic writing about the Colorado mountains really drew me in. <br /><br />The main idea behind this story is this: there are people out there with extra sensory abilities unique to each person. These people are like a secret race of people that "normal people" are not aware of. They all have one perfect match to themselves, called a soul seeker. This is like a soulmate but it's literally their other half who was born around the same day and who they spend all their lives searching for. This concept intrigues me. Imagine if all of us poor, indecisive people could know instantly when meeting someone that they would complement us like no other and make us happy for a lifetime...without a shadow of a doubt? It boggles the mind. Then again, the impossibility of finding that ONE person out of the whole planet is kind of staggering. And knowing that your perfect mate is out there kind of prevents any kind of recreational dating. <br /><br />I fell in love with Zed, the tough, brooding, motorcycle riding hero of the story. He is definitely stand-offish with Sky. Until she unintentionally speaks back to him telepathically(this is what alerts them that they have found their soulseeker). From this point on, he's ecstatic, euphoric, protective, and possessive. The problem is that Sky is adopted and is not aware of her powers or even what a soul seeker is. <br /><br />There is an amazing cast of characters that are just as well thought out as the main characters. Zed's family is funny, loving, and extremely supportive of Zed and I can't wait to read some of the other brothers stories and see them find their own perfect other halves. <br /><br />To anyone who loves PNR, I would highly recommend this book. It had romance, a little suspense, wonderful characters, and a very fascinating story. I Loved it! I will be reading the next book in the series very soon.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12880984748444021816" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer403071243" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17443285075468983717"><b>To read a proper review for Finding Sky as well as other reviews, go to my blog; <a href='http://drugscalledbooks.blogspot.co.il/2012/10/mini-review-finding-sky-by-joss-stirling.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Drugs Called Books</a>!</b><br/><br/>So, I loved this book. Zed and Sky are so cute together! He is simply adorable! It was funny and the romance was just so cute!! Definitely a good read.<br/>I do have some complaints, though.<br/>It had what I call a "weak beginning". It wasn't that it wasn't interesting, it just didn't manage to grab me and I found myself wondering from the story, often having to read one paragraph twice. After she met Zed </span>
  <span id="freeText17443285075468983717" style="display:none"><b>To read a proper review for Finding Sky as well as other reviews, go to my blog; <a href="http://drugscalledbooks.blogspot.co.il/2012/10/mini-review-finding-sky-by-joss-stirling.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Drugs Called Books</a>!</b><br /><br />So, I loved this book. Zed and Sky are so cute together! He is simply adorable! It was funny and the romance was just so cute!! Definitely a good read.<br />I do have some complaints, though.<br />It had what I call a "weak beginning". It wasn't that it wasn't interesting, it just didn't manage to grab me and I found myself wondering from the story, often having to read one paragraph twice. After she met Zed things picked up a bit and near the end they were simply great.<br />I had a hard time getting used to Sky's speech at the beginning. As part of her traits, she uses a lot of metaphors and the whole making things into stories. There were some beautifully written stuff, but I had to get used to the way her brain worked. It's not really a complaint, because that just who Sky is and later on, when Zed grounded her, we got much less of those. <br />I also didn't like that at first she kept calling them Gods and Mortals. I don't know why, but the once or twice she did that didn't rub well with me.<br />I did love Sky's personality, and I loved Zed. He was just the best &lt;3 at first I didn't like him, but then he turned sweet!! It was so refreshing to see a hero who didn't shy from his feelings; once he fell in love with her, he told her so. He just put it out there, and was so patient with--well, everything.<br />I do think they make an incredible couple.<br />Now, some technical annoyance; the summary, at least the one here on Goodreads, revealed too much of the story. I would've liked to have been more surprised :/</span>

<div id="review_295779257" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/295779257" />
    <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth"><img alt="Sarah Elizabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328957304p2/7591340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/295779257?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Elizabeth" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth">Sarah Elizabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=b4r">b4r</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=read-2012">read-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=r2r-complete">r2r-complete</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=as">as</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer295779257" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8302929135352255705">(I was given this book for free on a read-to-review basis.)<br/>16-year-old Sky has issues. She can’t remember much of her life before the age of 10, not even her real name. Dumped on the streets at the age of six, she can’t remember much before she was adopted by Sally and Simon her new parents, and if she’s honest she doesn’t really want to remember.<br/><br/>Now Sky finds herself in a new country and a new school. Her parents have just accepted new jobs in America, and she’s had to move with them, from Lond</span>
  <span id="freeText8302929135352255705" style="display:none">(I was given this book for free on a read-to-review basis.)<br />16-year-old Sky has issues. She can’t remember much of her life before the age of 10, not even her real name. Dumped on the streets at the age of six, she can’t remember much before she was adopted by Sally and Simon her new parents, and if she’s honest she doesn’t really want to remember.<br /><br />Now Sky finds herself in a new country and a new school. Her parents have just accepted new jobs in America, and she’s had to move with them, from London to Colorado.<br /><br />All is not lost though as Sky begins to make new friends, and also attracts the attention of Zed Benedict, the schools resident motorcycle-riding bad boy. Zed is not what he seems either though- Zed is a savant – he can talk with other savants telepathically, and he can even see a limited view of the future.<br /><br />Sky is in for a shock though when Zed tells her that she too is a savant, and not just any savant, but Zed’s soulfinder – his other half.<br /><br /><br />I really enjoyed this book. Everyone was just so normal – even the ones with superpowers! Sky was really down-to-earth, and I don’t know how anyone could fail to fall in love with Zed. Not only was he a bad boy but deep down he was a total sweetheart, and really tried his hardest to keep Sky safe, without pushing the whole soulfinder thing on her too strongly.<br /><br />The mystery surrounding Sky’s past was just right, and kept you interested and wondering what the secret was, and the mystery surrounding Zed’s family, although unexpected was actually a nice touch. <br /><br />Overall – a good young adult romance,<br />7 out of 10.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8302929135352255705" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16763579027857394904">Akhem. Finding Sky is one of the novels that could be a total hit, but is totally bland instead.<br/><br/>Sky is a girl with dark and pushed away from memory past. When she moves to US and meets the guy who claims to be her other half, she keeps it low, fights the danger, relieves her memory, blah, blah, add the paranormal bit, blah. <br/><br/>Akhem.   <span id="freeText16763579027857394904" style="display:none">Akhem. Finding Sky is one of the novels that could be a total hit, but is totally bland instead.<br /><br />Sky is a girl with dark and pushed away from memory past. When she moves to US and meets the guy who claims to be her other half, she keeps it low, fights the danger, relieves her memory, blah, blah, add the paranormal bit, blah. <br /><br />Akhem. Obviously, there is a pattern in the story, so there is little surprise for a reader. It reminds me of the very repetitive historical romances where the book won't end before the heroine is saved. Lovey-dovey stuff is absolutely irritating and I found myself eye-rolling way too often. I'd easily wave it all off but it was the tiny details that annoyed me the most. Like, how do you know what flowers are your favourite to get if you've never been given any? How do you know your boyfriend's mom's name if you've just been introduced to each other? And why, for God's sake, are your conversations so unrealistic and unintelligent?<br /><br />Just so you know, I'm not <i>completely</i> mean. I <i>did</i> try to find the good points of the book and here they are: there are witty parts to enjoy and it's a fast read. Which is fortunate if your eyes roll over without your control while reading it, after all we don't want to twist the little eye muscles, do we?</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_126518128" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/126518128" />
    <a title="Zoë Marriott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1975715-zo-marriott"><img alt="Zoë Marriott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496140905p2/1975715.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/126518128?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zoë Marriott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zoë Marriott" href="/user/show/1975715-zo-marriott">Zoë Marriott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer126518128" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12415400406848748754">THE SYNOPSIS: <br/><br/>You have half our gifts, I have the other . . . When English girl Sky, catches a glimpse of bad boy Zed in her new American high school, she can't get him out of her head. He talks to her with his thoughts. He reads her mind. He is the boy she will love for ever. Dark shadows stalk her past but a new evil threatens her future. Sky must face the dark even if it means losing her heart. <br/><br/>THE REVIEW: <br/><br/>I'd probably give this one 3.5 or 3.75. It's an entertaining and competently written ad</span>
  <span id="freeText12415400406848748754" style="display:none">THE SYNOPSIS: <br /><br />You have half our gifts, I have the other . . . When English girl Sky, catches a glimpse of bad boy Zed in her new American high school, she can't get him out of her head. He talks to her with his thoughts. He reads her mind. He is the boy she will love for ever. Dark shadows stalk her past but a new evil threatens her future. Sky must face the dark even if it means losing her heart. <br /><br />THE REVIEW: <br /><br />I'd probably give this one 3.5 or 3.75. It's an entertaining and competently written addition to the over-crowded paranormal romance genre, which, despite my well-honed cynicism, I found surprisingly touching.<br /><br />Sixteen year old Sky Bright (cringe) and her wacky artistic adopted parents move from the UK to a small ski town in Colorado for their work. Sky initially comes across as mentally fragile and vulnerable, with fractured and buried memories from a traumatic early childhood and years in foster care. Although she's happy with her parents, she's unhappy about the move, uncertain if it will be possible for her to fit in so far from home.<br /><br />However, it soon becomes clear that although Sky may be cute, tiny and shy (and saddled with a name so twee that even the other character's repeated mocking of it doesn't make me forgive the author), she's anything but a fluffy bunny. Beneath her shyness and the scars caused by her past, she shows intelligence and courage, and these develop, along with her supernatural powers, thoughout the story, making her a sympathetic and worthy lead.<br /><br />The romantic lead of the story, Zed, starts out as a something of a stereotype (leather-clad bad boy with a mean attitude and a permanent sneer, as Sky points out) but shakes off the bad-boy image fairly early on. His own emotional vulnerability due to his family's work is a welcome added dimension, and his unashamed 'soppiness' makes me like him, but I still didn't feel that I got to know him as well as Sky. I'm told there may be more installments (and in fact despite the plot resolution the story feels pretty open-ended) in which case I look forward to getting to see Zed in action as something more than a typical over-protective boyfriend. <br /><br />The secondary characters here are excellent, ranging from the well-developed artistic parents with their absent-minded yet shiningly sincere love for their daughter, to Sky's best friends who each have their own quirks and ambitions, to Zed's family who (what with two parents and seven brothers) got the short end of the straw when it came to development despite being some of the most intriguing people in the story (I heart Uriel).<br /><br />The spooky tone of the blurb led me to expect a certain kind of story, one with some horrific elements, but the plot of FINDING SKY is really more of a conventional action story than fantasy. The talents exhibited by the villains were seriously creepy, but after a strong introduction the implications were played down to the point that they felt almost extraneous. The same effects could have been achieved, as one character later suggests, by drugs or hypnotism. This may have been a deliberate choice on the author or her editor's part, but it seemed a shame to me. I like to be freaked out. Still, it at least it wasn't vampires or werewolves behind all the shenanigans - it's nice to see humans getting a good innings for once! <br /><br />The main reason my rating isn't higher for this one is that I felt that the story kept me at something of a distance. My friends and I were recently talking about how sometimes when you're working on a story you become convinced it's all too 'small' - that there's just nothing dramatic enough going on to justify a full book. This book displays the opposite problem. Although the prose is polished and notably lacking in the annoying romantic cliches that plague much paranormal YA writing, the lack of sensory detail made events that should have been terrifying and dramatic feel 'small', and rather far away. Ms Stirling seems to be a debut author which leads me to hope further books in the series may improve in this department and give me the thrills I'm truly longing for.<br /><br />In any case, if you're in the mood for a YA paranormal romance that doesn't drive you up the wall with unneccessary angst, a 2D sparkly hero or a TSTL heroine, FINDING SKY may be a refreshing read for you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12415400406848748754" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Ur143ONOWzP1EmDOhX5SYPbR4/5AwavH+EQ9K96LQh8jTo3DO7oq5R526egp27/LEJveEpkOlFjDCuprFU+wig==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UM+flM16adFDm/RScYNsjDZp5UqDJYWjYFkpZFpvz5IhPGqLFY4YB6j/fXTdJoEn0CPYplrqujxbF/4kkas9Bw==')})
  }

Marked as special at an early age, Jacinda knows her every move is watched. But she longs for freedom to make her own choices. When she breaks the most sacred tenet among her kind, she nearly pays with her life. Until a beautiful stranger saves her. A stranger who was sent to hunt those like her. For Jacinda is a draki, a descendant of dragons whose greatest defense is her secret ability to shift into human form. Forced to flee into the mortal world with her family, Jacinda struggles to adapt to her new surroundings. The only bright light is Will. Gorgeous, elusive Will who stirs her inner draki to life. Although she is irresistibly drawn to him, Jacinda knows Will\'s dark secret: He and his family are hunters. She should avoid him at all costs. But her inner draki is slowly slipping away;if it dies she will be left as a human forever. She\'ll do anything to prevent that. Even if it means getting closer to her most dangerous enemy. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9028942683013709438">Joss Stirling is a British novelist. Her first novel under this name was the internationally successful, Finding Sky, which is followed by five others in the same series entering into the savant world of young people with special powers. Central to the story are the Benedict Brothers, seven talented guys from Colorado. <br/><br/>In a second series, Struck, Joss begins a new world of detective romance. The f</span>
  <span id="freeText9028942683013709438" style="display:none">Joss Stirling is a British novelist. Her first novel under this name was the internationally successful, Finding Sky, which is followed by five others in the same series entering into the savant world of young people with special powers. Central to the story are the Benedict Brothers, seven talented guys from Colorado. <br /><br />In a second series, Struck, Joss begins a new world of detective romance. The first three parts are: Struck (#1) and Stung (#2), and Shaken (#3) and Scorched (#4). Joss introduces readers to four new heroes - Kieran Storm, Nathan Hunter, Joe Masters and Damien Castle, who all attention the Young Detective Agency. The first part, Struck, won the Romantic Novel of the Year 2015 in the UK.<br /><br />Her new series, PERIL, a paranormal love story set in the near future, is out 13 July 2017.<br /><br />Joss lives in Oxford, England. She is married with three children.<br /><br /><br />Stirling also publishes under two pen names: Julia Golding and Eve Edwards.</span>
